     935                 :            : /* Return a stream for FILE, opened with mode HOW.  A null FILE means
     936                 :            :    standard output; HOW should be "w".  When opening for input, "-"
     937                 :            :    means standard input.  To avoid confusion, do not return file
     938                 :            :    descriptors STDIN_FILENO, STDOUT_FILENO, or STDERR_FILENO when
     939                 :            :    opening an ordinary FILE.  Return NULL if unsuccessful.
     940                 :            : 
     941                 :            :    fadvise() is used to specify an access pattern for input files.
     942                 :            :    There are a few hints we could possibly provide,
     943                 :            :    and after careful testing it was decided that
     944                 :            :    specifying POSIX_FADV_SEQUENTIAL was not detrimental
     945                 :            :    to any cases.  On Linux 2.6.31, this option doubles
     946                 :            :    the size of read ahead performed and thus was seen to
     947                 :            :    benefit these cases:
     948                 :            :      Merging
     949                 :            :      Sorting with a smaller internal buffer
     950                 :            :      Reading from faster flash devices
     951                 :            : 
     952                 :            :    In _addition_ one could also specify other hints...
     953                 :            : 
     954                 :            :    POSIX_FADV_WILLNEED was tested, but Linux 2.6.31
     955                 :            :    at least uses that to _synchronously_ prepopulate the cache
     956                 :            :    with the specified range.  While sort does need to
     957                 :            :    read all of its input before outputting, a synchronous
     958                 :            :    read of the whole file up front precludes any processing
     959                 :            :    that sort could do in parallel with the system doing
     960                 :            :    read ahead of the data. This was seen to have negative effects
     961                 :            :    in a couple of cases:
     962                 :            :      Merging
     963                 :            :      Sorting with a smaller internal buffer
     964                 :            :    Note this option was seen to shorten the runtime for sort
     965                 :            :    on a multicore system with lots of RAM and other processes
     966                 :            :    competing for CPU.  It could be argued that more explicit
     967                 :            :    scheduling hints with `nice` et. al. are more appropriate
     968                 :            :    for this situation.
     969                 :            : 
     970                 :            :    POSIX_FADV_NOREUSE is a possibility as it could lower
     971                 :            :    the priority of input data in the cache as sort will
     972                 :            :    only need to process it once.  However its functionality
     973                 :            :    has changed over Linux kernel versions and as of 2.6.31
     974                 :            :    it does nothing and thus we can't depend on what it might
     975                 :            :    do in future.
     976                 :            : 
     977                 :            :    POSIX_FADV_DONTNEED is not appropriate for user specified
     978                 :            :    input files, but for temp files we do want to drop the
     979                 :            :    cache immediately after processing.  This is done implicitly
     980                 :            :    however when the files are unlinked.  */
     981                 :            :

    4141                 :            : 
    4142                 :            : /* Sort lines, possibly in parallel.  The arguments are as in struct
    4143                 :            :    thread_args above.
    4144                 :            : 
    4145                 :            :    The algorithm has three phases: node creation, sequential sort,
    4146                 :            :    and binary merge.
    4147                 :            : 
    4148                 :            :    During node creation, sortlines recursively visits each node in the
    4149                 :            :    binary merge tree and creates a NODE structure corresponding to all the
    4150                 :            :    future line merging NODE is responsible for. For each call to
    4151                 :            :    sortlines, half the available threads are assigned to each recursive
    4152                 :            :    call, until a leaf node having only 1 available thread is reached.
    4153                 :            : 
    4154                 :            :    Each leaf node then performs two sequential sorts, one on each half of
    4155                 :            :    the lines it is responsible for. It records in its NODE structure that
    4156                 :            :    there are two sorted sublists available to merge from, and inserts its
    4157                 :            :    NODE into the priority queue.
    4158                 :            : 
    4159                 :            :    The binary merge phase then begins. Each thread drops into a loop
    4160                 :            :    where the thread retrieves a NODE from the priority queue, merges lines
    4161                 :            :    available to that NODE, and potentially insert NODE or its parent back
    4162                 :            :    into the queue if there are sufficient available lines for them to
    4163                 :            :    merge. This continues until all lines at all nodes of the merge tree
    4164                 :            :    have been merged. */
